People v. Superior Court (memorial Medical Center)


Nos. B056780, B057129


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


234 Cal. App. 3d 363; 286 Cal. Rptr. 478; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1106; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7774; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11852



September 24, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The petition of real party in interest for review by the Supreme Court was denied December 19, 1991. Mosk, J., and Panelli, J., were of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BH000107, William R. Pounders, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing the superior court to vacate its order of February 1, 1991, modifying the property to be seized under the search warrant sought by petitioner, the People of the State of California, and further directing that the superior court enter a new and different order granting the People the right to obtain the property listed in the statement of property to be seized.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order, by writ of mandate, to compel respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), to vacate its order that modified the property to be seized from real party in interest hospital in a criminal action against one of the hospital's physicians. Real party in interest sought a writ of mandate, contending that the modified order was still an abuse of discretion over privileged records.


OVERVIEW: The state sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent trial court to vacate its order modifying the state's original statement of property to be seized from real property in interest hospital. Real party in interest also sought a writ, under the modified warrant, contending that the records to be seized were protected from discovery, and therefore the trial court abused its discretion in issuing the modified order. The documents pertained to an investigation arising from two separate incidents of possible criminally negligent behavior by a physician. Real party in interest argued that the documents were privileged pursuant to a peer review statute. The court held that privileges were to be narrowly construed since they prevented the admission of relevant and otherwise admissible evidence, and could obstruct the attainment of justice. The writ was issued to reverse the order, where the records and proceedings of real party in interest's peer review committees were subject to discovery in a criminal action.


OUTCOME: The writ of mandate was granted to respondent trial court to vacate its order modifying property to be seized, because the peer review privilege did not protect the records and documents of real party in interest hospital's peer review committee from discovery in a criminal action.

 

1223 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of Sutter v. Davis


No. C007363


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


234 Cal. App. 3d 319; 285 Cal. Rptr. 736; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1102; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7686; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11675



September 23, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sutter County, No. P896, Robert W. Steel, Robert C. Lenhard ++ and Thomas L. Hill, ** Judges.


++ Retired judge of the Sutter Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.


** Judge of the Yuba Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Sutter County (California) that denied defendant's request for a jury trial in a paternity action brought by plaintiff county to establish paternity and reimbursement for public assistance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county filed this action against defendant to establish paternity and obtain child support and reimbursement for public assistance. Defendant denied paternity and requested a jury trial on the issue. He also stipulated to a blood test and the appointment of a blood test expert. County challenged defendant's request for jury trial. The trial court concluded that there was no right to a jury trial in a paternity action in California, whether by state or federal constitutional mandate or by statute. In a bench trial, defendant's paternity was established. The issue on appeal was whether a defendant in a paternity action had a right to a jury trial. The court held that there was to be a balance of the action's features and the private interests and consequences against the state's interest in not providing a right to a jury trial in the action. The judgment was affirmed because the interests and consequences implicated in a paternity action were not as great as the interest and consequences implicated in the interest of personal liberty and those actions mandating a due process right to jury trial.


OUTCOME: The order that denied defendant's request for a jury trial in a paternity action brought by plaintiff county was affirmed because a right to a jury trial in a paternity action did not exist in the state pursuant to statute or common law.

 

1224 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Sacramento Cable TV v. City of Sacramento


No. C008372


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


234 Cal. App. 3d 232; 286 Cal. Rptr. 470; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1146; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8020; 91 Daily Journal DAR 12190; 19 Media L. Rep. 1532



September 20, 1991 


NOTICE:  [***1] Ordered Published October 1, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: A petition for a rehearing was denied October 16, 1991, and appellants' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied January 16, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 510433, Jeffrey L. Gunther, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, cable company and individual, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court, Sacramento County (California) which dismissed plaintiffs' challenge to a tax imposed by defendant city on the users of a cable television service.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, cable company and individual, contended that the tax imposed by defendant city violated U.S. Const. amend I. Plaintiffs argued that the tax implicated U.S. Const. amend. I because it treated cable television differently from other protected speakers. The court held that the tax was not imposed solely on cable television but actually covered the use of telephone, gas, and electric services. The court stated that the question was whether defendant could classify cable television for purposes of taxation with telephone, gas, and electric utilities. The court stated that much like the public utilities, cable television service was transmitted to customers through structures located in or on public easements created expressly for utility access. Cable television operators, like public utilities, were regulated by the Public Utilities Commission with respect to the operation and construction of facilities and equipment to ensure health and safety. The court affirmed, holding that there was a significant degree of commonality among these four services and the grouping of cable television with the three utilities was rationally based.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the challenge of plaintiffs, cable company and individual, to a tax imposed on users of cable television service was affirmed. The court held that the grouping of cable television service with other public utilities was rationally based.

 

1225 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Hebert v. Los Angeles Raiders, Ltd.


No. B057462.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


23 Cal. App. 4th 414; 29 Cal. Rptr. 2d 540; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1067; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11438; 1991-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P69,606



September 17, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 12, 1991 (S023546)
Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 234 Cal. App. 3d 36 and 6 Cal. App. 4th 184 and 12 Cal. App. 4th 904 and 18 Cal. App. 4th 165.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC-012505, Charles E. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff football player appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that dismissed his complaint against defendants, professional football team and league, that alleged that defendants' system of anti-competition restrained him from engaging in his lawful profession, trade, or business in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, §1, and Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 16600.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff football player challenged the trial court judgment that dismissed his complaint against defendants, professional football team and league, sustaining defendants' demurrer on the grounds that the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, precluded application of California's antitrust law, the Cartwright Act, Bus. & Prof. Code, § 16700 et seq., to professional football. Plaintiff claimed that defendants' anti-competition system, known as Plan B, illegally and unconstitutionally restrained him from engaging in his lawful profession in violation of Cal. Const. art. I, §1 and the Cartwright Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 16600. Defendants claimed that the appeal was moot, but the court found that the appeal raised an important issue that was likely to recur, yet evade review. The court affirmed the trial court judgment, holding that the commerce clause defense was properly raised and determined by way of demurrer. The court held that it was bound by precedent that found the burden on interstate commerce outweighed California's interests in applying its antitrust laws to the player-team-league relationships. The court also found denial of leave to amend was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment dismissing plaintiff football player's complaint against defendants, professional football team and league, holding that it was bound by the California Supreme Court decision that held that the commerce clause of the U.S. Constitution precluded application of California's antitrust law to professional football.

 

1226 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ciani v. San Diego Trust & Sav. Bank


No. D015057


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


233 Cal. App. 3d 1604; 285 Cal. Rptr. 699; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1061; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7418; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11309



September 12, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 3, 1991, Reported at 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1154, and respondents' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 639857, Barbara T. Gamer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Based upon our review of the evidence submitted to the trial court, and to some extent augmented by material filed in our court, we must conclude that (1) the notice given under section 65956 was insufficient to cause activation of the coastal development permit by operation of law, and (2) that even were we wrong in this conclusion no notice of the deemed approved permit was given upon its becoming effective sufficient to start an appeals period running. In the state of the present record, therefore, we conclude that the effective permit obtained by the Trust is that issued by the City on July 10. Assuming this to be the case, the presently pending appeal to the Coastal Commission was timely filed, and the superior court is obliged to continue in force the restraint against further demolition. We are mindful, however, that we deal with facts tentatively found, upon the basis of probably incomplete evidence; and [***2] that the superior court upon further hearings and in light of additional evidence may find it appropriate to modify the restraining order presently in effect. In light of the present status of affairs, we are obliged to issue the writ of supersedeas, the result of which is to overrule the trial court's denial of the preliminary injunction. Our order is that the stay of demolition, previously imposed by this court and now in force, shall continue in force until the superior court issues a new ruling. This order does not preclude the superior court from holding further proceedings and from issuing such new preliminary injunctive relief, or a new order denying such relief, as may be in harmony with the above opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, petitioners, an individual and the California Coastal Commission, appealed a ruling of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), denying petitioners an order preliminarily enjoining respondent bank, as trustee, from continuing to demolish structures located on the trust's land, pending a determination of whether certain development permits were properly issued or, if issued, had gone into effect.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, an individual and an agency that regulated coastal development, filed suits, later consolidated, against respondent bank, as trustee, to halt demolition of buildings on land owned by the trust, because respondent did not have the required permits, including one from petitioner agency. When action was not taken on respondent's application to petitioner agency, respondent invoked the Permit Streamlining Act, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 65921 et seq., to obtain automatic approval, and began demolition. Petitioners obtained a temporary restraining order, but the lower court later denied a preliminary injunction, and petitioners appealed for a supersedeas writ. The court found that respondent had not complied with notice requirements that were prerequisite to obtaining the permit under the Streamlining Act; that, even if respondent had obtained the permit, the permit remained subject to a ten-day waiting period, and to certain appeal provisions applicable to all such permits; and that petitioners' challenge to the issuance of the permit was timely. The court issued the supersedeas writ, thereby overruling the lower court's order denying preliminary relief.


OUTCOME: The court issued a supersedeas writ, overruling the lower court's denial of a motion by petitioners, an individual and the California Coastal Commission, for an order preliminarily enjoining respondent bank, as trustee, from continuing certain demolition on the trust's land, based on respondent's alleged failure to give notice concerning its application for, and receipt of, a required development permit from petitioner agency.

 

1227 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Johnson


No. E007984


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two


233 Cal. App. 3d 1541; 285 Cal. Rptr. 394; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1046; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7361; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11207



September 11, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied December 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-28958, George G. Grover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which convicted defendant of first-degree burglary and imposed a five-year enhancement under Cal. Penal Code § 667(a), for a prior serious felony conviction in a foreign state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for burglary of an inhabited dwelling was reversed on appeal because the trial court, in taking defendant's guilty plea, failed to advise him of his privilege against self-incrimination. On remand, defendant was found guilty of first-degree burglary. In a bifurcated proceeding, the trial court found true the allegation of a prior serious felony conviction and sentenced defendant for the burglary with a consecutive five-year term for the prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 667. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, finding the sentence proper although the previous conviction occurred in another state. The prior indictment charged conduct that would have unequivocally constituted a serious felony under California law, defendant was found guilty as charged, and the record supported the finding that the elements that were adjudicated included personal use of a deadly weapon. Under those circumstances, the court found no violation of equal protection in the use of the prior conviction as the basis for an enhancement.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that imposed a five-year sentencing enhancement for a prior serious felony conviction in another state was affirmed. No violation of equal protection occurred because the prior conviction involved conduct that would have constituted a serious felony under state law, including the use of a weapon.

 

1228 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brewer


No. A051318.


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four.


233 Cal. App. 3d 1440; 285 Cal. Rptr. 225; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1025; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7334; 91 Daily Journal DAR 11083



September 9, 1991.


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted October 8, 1991 (See 235 Cal. App. 3d 909)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 92207, Michael E. Ballachey, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which granted the motion of defendant to suppress the evidence of rock cocaine seized from his person during a patdown search initiated by a police officer after detaining defendant for a violation of Oakland, Cal., Municipal Ord. § 3-4.21, which prohibited the possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages on public property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained by a police officer for violating Oakland, Cal., Municipal Ord. § 3-4.21, which prohibited the possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages on public property. The officer then conducted a patdown search of defendant, based upon the officer's knowledge that the location was a known narcotics area and that a nearby hotel housed numerous parolees of violent crimes. The officer discovered a baggie that contained rock cocaine, and defendant was charged with possessing cocaine base in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11350. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the narcotics, and the motion was granted. The state appealed pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1238(a)(7). The court reversed the order that suppressed the evidence, finding that while that portion of the ordinance that prohibited possession of alcoholic beverages was preempted by state law, the remainder of the ordinance was severable. Thus, the police officer was entitled to rely upon it to initiate the detention of defendant. The court concluded that after deleting the objectionable portions of the ordinance, the remainder was capable of independent existence and was valid in its own right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence of rock cocaine seized from his person while he was detained for violating an ordinance that prohibited the possession or consumption of alcoholic beverages on public property. The court found that, while state law preempted a portion of the ordinance, the remaining portion was severable and valid.

 

1229 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Tahoe Reg'l Planning Agency v. King


No. C005345


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


233 Cal. App. 3d 1365; 285 Cal. Rptr. 335; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1023; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7290; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10986



September 6, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied October 4, 1991, and respondents' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of El Dorado County, No. SLT1587, Lloyd B. Hamilton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the case is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. Costs to TRPA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant regional planning agency challenged the order of the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), which granted respondent's motion for summary judgment, denied appellant's motion for summary judgment, and declared a portion of appellant's sign ordinance invalid. Appellant had sought declaratory and injunctive relief to remove billboards belonging to respondent owners.


OVERVIEW: Appellant regional planning agency tried to remove billboards belonging to respondent owners that did not comply with the appellant's sign ordinances. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondents, declaring the ordinance did not pay compensation as directed by the Highway Beautification Act (HBA), 23 U.S.C.S. § 131, and unconstitutionally took property rights without payment. Upon review, the court concluded that the HBA did not preempt appellant's authority or create a right to compensation, because Congress had created a narrow exception to the HBA. Holding the ordinance was constitutional if applied only to commercial advertising, the court ruled that esthetic preservation was a legitimate use of the police power. Therefore, examination of many factors was needed to determine if the ordinance was an unconstitutional "taking", such as: was the regulation so onerous that reasonable use was denied; was the amortization schedule which allowed respondents to recover expenses reasonable; was the state interest substantially advanced by the ordinance. The court held that summary judgment was inappropriate and remanded because an extensive factual inquiry was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for respondent owners and remanded because the issue of whether appellant regional planning agency's sign ordinance was valid required extensive factual inquiry as to the economic impact on the respondents and the degree that a legitimate interest of the state would be advanced. The court also found no preemption by the Highway Beautification Act.

 

1230 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


City of Los Angeles v. Chadwick


No. B054922.


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One.


233 Cal. App. 3d 1296; 285 Cal. Rptr. 191; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1021; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7228; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10912



September 5, 1991, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 7, 1991, Reported at 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1160.
Review Denied December 12, 1991 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).
Mosk J., is of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C 520461, Victor E. Chavez and Jack T. Ryburn, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed a judgment and final order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which condemned plaintiff's real property on behalf of defendant city under the Eminent Domain Law, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1230.010 et seq. Plaintiff alleged he was denied statutory and procedural due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city decided to condemn plaintiff owner's real property under the Eminent Domain Law, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1230.010 et seq., seven years before plaintiff was given formal or actual notice. The trial court denied plaintiff's claim of deprivation of statutory and due process rights and plaintiff appealed. The court reversed, holding that the Eminent Domain Law required notice before issuing the "resolution of necessity" under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1240.030, and that the resolution was not valid because it was influenced by gross abuse of defendant's discretion. The court found defendant abused its discretion because there was a total lack of substantial evidence supporting the resolution, and, at the time of the hearing to determine the necessity of the taking, defendant had irrevocably committed itself to the taking, regardless of what evidence might be presented. The court remanded for a new determination of present day value because, although plaintiff had not contested the valuation, the fact that defendant had already redeveloped the property made it the only practical and financially realistic remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the final order of the trial court which condemned plaintiff owner's real property under the Eminent Domain Law because defendant city's decision to condemn the property before giving notice or opportunity to oppose the action was abusive of its authority and deprived the plaintiff of his statutory and due process rights. The cause was remanded for a new, present day valuation of the property as the only available remedy.

 

1231 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gandara


No. F014516.


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


233 Cal. App. 3d 1163; 284 Cal. Rptr. 906; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 989; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7016; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10722



August 29, 1991.


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted November 14, 1991 (S023293)
Trans. January 30, 1992 to Ct. App., 5th Dist., with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of Whitman v. Superior Court (1991) 54 Cal. 3d 1063.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kern County, No. 42750, James M. Stuart, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the order from the Superior Court of Kern County (California), that found Cal. Evid. Code § 872(b) (1990) did not authorize the admission of multiple hearsay at a preliminary hearing and granted defendant's Cal. Penal Code § 995 motion and dismissed the information.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's preliminary examination, the magistrate permitted a police officer to testify as to the content of a laboratory report and admitted into evidence the curriculum vita of the criminalist that prepared the report. The magistrate overruled defendant's objection to the admission of the multiple hearsay. Defendant was charged by information with transportation of heroin and possession for sale of heroin. Defendant sought to dismiss the information pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 995 because Cal. Evid. Code § 872(b) (1990) did not authorize the admission of multiple hearsay at the preliminary hearing. The trial court granted defendant's motion and dismissed the information. The state sought review. The appellate court held that § 872(b) required the officer who related the hearsay to have a certain amount of training and experience. However, no training or experience was required to relate the laboratory report or provide the criminalist's qualifications. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the admission of multiple hearsay at defendant's preliminary hearing did not come under an exception to the hearsay rule and was not authorized by § 872(b).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the information against defendant because the admission of multiple hearsay at defendant's preliminary hearing was not statutorily authorized and did not fall under an exception to the hearsay rule.

 

1232 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Kavanau v. Santa Monica Rent Control Bd.


No. B049032.


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven.


233 Cal. App. 3d 1095; 284 Cal. Rptr. 889; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 987; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7043; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10626



August 28, 1991.


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 14, 1991 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at 1991 Cal. LEXIS 5148.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C735953, Edward M. Ross, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his petition for a peremptory writ of mandate to order respondent rent control board to permit him to implement all of the rent increase to which respondent found he was entitled.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landlord filed an application with respondent rent control board in which he requested that, on a permanent basis, he be allowed to raise rents in order to keep up with the rise in his expenses, and that he be allowed a temporary rent increase as reimbursement for certain current and proposed capital improvements. Respondent granted his application, but phased the increase in over a period of five or six years. Appellant sought review, contending that respondent's action was confiscatory and unconstitutional. The trial court affirmed respondent's decision, and denied appellant's motion for a peremptory writ of mandate. Affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that phasing in appellant's increase so that rents were not raised more than the 12 percent per annum allowed by the rent control ordinance did not deprive appellant of his constitutionally guaranteed just and reasonable return. The court further held that the rent control formula represented a rational attempt to accommodate the conflicting interests of protecting tenants from burdensome rent increases while at the same time ensuring that landlords were guaranteed a fair return on investment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment requiring appellant landlord's increase to be phased in over several years because it was wholly consistent with the purposes and provisions of the rent control ordinance to require landlords to wait a few years to recapture the full cost of expensive repairs and improvements in order to cushion the financial impact on their tenants.

 

1233 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Sanford v. Garamendi


No. C006971


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


233 Cal. App. 3d 1109; 284 Cal. Rptr. 897; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 990; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7010; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10639



August 28, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] A petition for a rehearing was denied September 23, 1991, and appellants' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 14, 1991. Mosk, J., was of the opinion that the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 360783, James Timothy Ford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed insofar as it denies plaintiffs' request for a writ of mandate commanding the Commissioner to cease granting insurance license applications to banks and to rescind any such license previously issued to banks. The judgment is otherwise reversed and the matter remanded to the trial court with directions to issue a writ of mandate commanding the Commissioner to cease granting insurance license applications to bank subsidiaries and to rescind any insurance license previously issued to any such entity. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individual insurance agents and brokers, and their trade association, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) that denied their petition for writ of mandate and complaint for declaratory relief to direct defendant insurance commissioner to rescind insurance agency and brokerage licenses issued to state banks because of the adoption of Proposition 103.


OVERVIEW: In 1988 Proposition 103 received a majority of the votes for passage. This proposition contained a provision that revoked Cal. Ins. Code § 1643, which prohibited banks, bank holding companies, and their subsidiaries and affiliated from being licensed as insurance agents or brokers. The superintendent of banks concluded that Proposition 103 impliedly repealed Cal. Ins. Code § 772(b) and Cal. Ins. Code §1208. Plaintiffs, individual insurance agents and brokers and their trade association challenged that decision. The court affirmed the trial court's decision holding that Proposition 103 intended to allow banks to engage in the insurance agency and brokerage business. The court reversed the trial court's decision and held that Proposition 103 did not impliedly revoke § 772 or § 1208 because neither the initiative, or the accompanying ballot materials suggested any application to bank subsidiaries. The court remanded with direction to issue a writ of mandate commanding defendant to cease granting insurance license applications to bank subsidiaries and to rescind any licenses previously issued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial courts determination that Proposition 103 allowed banks to engage in insurance and brokerage business, however, the court reversed the decision that the provisions that governed licensure to bank subsidiaries was impliedly repealed holding that these provisions were not involved with the proposition, and remained in effect.

 

1234 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



California Aviation, Inc. v. Leeds


No. B048101


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


233 Cal. App. 3d 724; 284 Cal. Rptr. 687; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 971; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6918; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10412



August 23, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified September 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. WEC122415, Edward Y. Kakita, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment. We remand the matter to the trial court with directions that it strike its earlier order granting Leeds's summary judgment, and enter a new order denying Leeds's summary judgment motion. CAI is entitled to its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent attorney in an action brought by appellant for malpractice.


OVERVIEW: After appellant client brought suit against respondent attorney for malpractice, the bankruptcy court granted appellant's request to convert his existing bankruptcy from Chapter 11 to Chapter 7. Thereafter, the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of respondent on the ground that the state's one-year statute of limitations had run. Appellant sought review, contending that the two-year federal statute of limitations applied pursuant to 11 U.S.C.S. § 108(a). On review, the court reversed the trial court's summary judgment. The court found that appellant had standing to bring the appeal in spite of the bankruptcy conversion and in spite of any express authorization by the trustee to bring the appeal, because the appeal was a continuation of the underlying suit. The court found that appellant had timely filed the malpractice suit because the federal bankruptcy extension statute, § 108(a), controlled the case and extended the limitations to two years from the time of appellant's Chapter 11 filing. The court also ruled that the bankruptcy conversion did not change the applicability of the federal statute and that the federal statute preempted the state's statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent attorney's summary judgment against appellant client's malpractice suit, because appellant had standing to bring the appeal and because the federal bankruptcy extension statute provided a two-year statute of limitations for appellant to bring the suit. The court noted that federal bankruptcy statute preempted the one-year state limitation period.

Hobbs v. Municipal Court


No. D013897


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One


233 Cal. App. 3d 670; 284 Cal. Rptr. 655; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 966; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6866; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10444



August 22, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petitioner's application for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 14, 1991. Mosk, J., was of the opinion that the application should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court for the San Diego Judicial District of San Diego County, No. 632480, Charles G. Rogers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a peremptory writ of mandate from the Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division One to rescind an order that authorized prosecutorial discovery pursuant to Proposition 115, Cal. Penal Code §§ 1054-1054.7.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with misdemeanor burglary. He sought a peremptory writ of mandate to rescind an order that authorized prosecutorial discovery subsequent to the passage of Proposition 115. The trial court denied the petition. The court denied and held that reciprocal discovery provisions of Proposition 115, Cal. Penal Code §§ 1054-1054.7, did not violate petitioner's federal and state constitutional rights of due process of law and assistance of counsel. The court also held that the provisions of Proposition 115 did not violate the work product doctrine, and that they applied to misdemeanor as well as felony cases.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a peremptory writ of mandate to rescind the trial court's order authorizing prosecutorial discovery. The court held that the state law providing for reciprocal discovery in criminal cases did not violate petitioner's rights to due process of law and assistance of counsel, and that it did not violate the work product doctrine. The court also held that the law applied to misdemeanor cases.

Colgate-Palmolive Co. v. Franchise Tax Bd.


No. C007044


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD DISTRICT


4 Cal. App. 4th 1681; 284 Cal. Rptr. 780; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 949; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10314



August 20, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Granted November 27, 1991 (S023147)
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 233 Cal.App.3d 855 and 4 Cal. App. 4th 1611.) (See 10 Cal. App. 4th 1768)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 319715, Robert Gardner, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment on the foreign commerce clause issue is reversed. The judgment on the constitutional and statutory distortion issues and on the matter of sanctions is affirmed. The Board is awarded its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, franchise tax board, challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Sacramento County (California), which determined that California's worldwide unitary tax method was unconstitutional, denied appellant's motion for discovery sanctions, and awarded certain costs to respondent domestic-parent corporation.


OVERVIEW: Respondent domestic-parent corporation was directed to pay additional taxes. Under protest, respondent paid the additional taxes and then filed suit on the ground that the additional taxes violated the foreign commerce clause. The trial determined that California's worldwide unitary tax method was unconstitutional. The court reversed the trial court's decision on the foreign commerce clause issue because the court determined that the tax method did not violate the foreign commerce clause in that there was not a substantial risk of multiple taxation, and the tax did not impair federal uniformity or prevent the federal government from speaking with one voice when regulating commercial relations with foreign governments. However, the court affirmed the trial court's decision in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision on the foreign commerce clause issue because the tax method did not violate the foreign commerce clause since there was not a substantial risk of multiple taxation, and the tax did not impair federal uniformity or prevent the federal government from speaking with one voice when regulating commercial relations with foreign governments.

 

1237 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


In re Wick


Nos. G010932, G010951.


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Three.


233 Cal. App. 3d 516; 285 Cal. Rptr. 676; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 947; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6637; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10108



August 15, 1991 


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified September 3, 1991.
Review Denied November 21, 1991 and Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).
Kennard, J. is of the opinion the petition should be granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. C-84422, Richard M. Aronson, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: (Pursuant to Cal. Const., art. VI, § 21.) Orders to show cause discharged; petitions denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Orange County (California), which denied bail after defendants were charged with first-degree murder with "special circumstances" pursuant to Cal. Penal Code §§ 190.2(a)(3), 190.2(a)(17)(i), and 190.2(a)(17)(vii).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with two counts of first-degree murder committed during the course of an armed robbery. The information alleged three "special circumstances." They were multiple murders pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(3), murder perpetrated in the commission of robbery, Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(17)(i), and murder perpetrated in the commission of burglary, Cal. Penal Code § 190.2(a)(17)(vii). The prosecution did not seek the death penalty. Defendants filed motions to set bail, but were denied because their cases were potentially capital cases. Defendants were later found guilty at trial, so the question was moot. However, the action involved a matter of continuing public interest, and the issue was likely to recur, so the court proceeded to the merits. The court held that although Cal. Const. art. I, § 12(a) provided that a person shall be released on bail except for "capital crimes" when the facts were evident or the presumption great, a court was no longer dealing with a capital case when the prosecutor elected not to seek the death penalty. Defendants were not facing "capital crimes" when the prosecution decided not to seek the death penalty.


OUTCOME: Although the proceedings were moot because defendants were already convicted at trial, the court chose to hear the case on the merits because the issue was likely to occur. The court held that defendants were not precluded from bail when the prosecution did not seek the death penalty because the cases were not deemed "capital crimes," and were thus not subject to bail preclusion.

 

1238 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Johnson


No. H005433


Court of Appeal of California, Sixth Appellate District


233 Cal. App. 3d 425; 284 Cal. Rptr. 579; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 940; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6525; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10092



August 14, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 116801, Frank Cliff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 116801 (California), which found him guilty of second-degree murder and first-degree murder in two separate trials, claiming that he received in effective assistance of counsel, evidence was improperly admitted, the prosecutor improperly impeached appellant's character, and the prosecutor engaged in vindictiveness by amending the charging instrument.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's girlfriend was reported missing by appellant. Years later, appellant married another individual, where they both sold illegal drugs. During his marriage, appellant physically fought with his wife, and threatened her, claiming that he would treat her the same as he did to his girlfriend. Appellant also went to a drug dealer's home, and shot an individual, whom he believed had stole his money. Appellant was eventually found guilty for murdering his girlfriend, and the drug dealer in two separate trials. Appellant challenged his convictions, and the court held that his wife's testimony did not violate the husband-wife privilege, as the testimony was previously made public, while he was in a criminal proceeding for committing a crime against his wife. The court also determined that there was no ineffective assistance of counsel, the prosecutor properly established the corpus delicti and correctly impeached appellant's character by his prior bad acts and prior convictions. The court further stated that the prosecutor did not engage in vindictiveness by amending the charging information, and evidence of appellant's abuse to his wife was properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant was properly convicted of two murders in separate trials, as the evidence was properly admitted; there was no violation of the husband-wife privilege; the prosecutor did not engage in vindictiveness by changing the indictment; appellant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel, and that appellant's character was correctly impeached by his prior convictions.

 

1239 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Howard v. Superior Court


No. A054030


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


233 Cal. App. 3d 1436; 285 Cal. Rptr. 127; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1016; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7227; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10956



August 14, 1991 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for Publication September 5, 1991


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 138883, Jack K. Berman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco to vacate its order denying Howard's motion and to reconsider the motion in light of the views expressed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner owner filed a peremptory writ of mandate from the decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied petitioner's request for the return of his handgun and concluded that under the circumstances the gun should be destroyed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner owner was the registered owner of a handgun. This was the same handgun mentioned in a police report by an off-duty police officer who heard three shots fired and saw the third party holding a recently fired gun as several people ran. The gun became an exhibit in the prosecution for possession of a firearm by a felon, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021. Petitioner moved for return of his handgun, but the trial court denied the motion. The court explained that the third party was a customer of petitioner, who was a bail bondsman, and that petitioner allowed his customers and friends to go into his back office. Evidently the gun was kept in the back office, and the third party took it without petitioner's knowledge. The court held that pursuant to the attorney general suggestion, it remanded the matter to the trial court to consider whether the handgun was stolen from petitioner, as he alleged.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate directing the trial court to vacate its order denying petitioner owner's motion for the return of his handgun. Upon remand, the trial court was to determine if the gun had been stolen.

 

1240 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Lucas Valley Homeowners Ass'n v. County of Marin


No. A049762


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Four


233 Cal. App. 3d 130; 284 Cal. Rptr. 427; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 932; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6440; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10005



August 12, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The petition of plaintiffs and respondents for review by the Supreme Court was denied October 31, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, No. 143527, William H. Stephens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment that directed the County and Board to vacate the resolution approving the conditional use permit and negative declaration. Parties are to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant religious organization challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which vacated a resolution adopted by a county government allowing appellant to convert a single-family residence into a neighborhood synagogue with associated uses, on the basis that the county granted appellant an impermissibly religious preference, and that the decision supporting the permit was not backed by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant religious organization applied to a county government for a use permit to convert a single-family residence into a neighborhood synagogue. The county granted the use permit, and respondents, local resident homeowners, challenged the ruling. The trial court vacated the county's resolution granting the permit, stating that appellant was unlawfully granted a religious preference, the findings for supporting the permit was not supported by substantial evidence, and an environmental impact report (EIR) was required. Appellant sought further review, and the court reversed the trial court. The court stated that inaccurate legal advice the court obtained was harmless error, as only the board's decision was relevant to the appeal. The court also determined that appellant was not granted an unconstitutional religious preference, and the county board's decision that the synagogue would not be detrimental from the point of view of parking, traffic, noise and property values was supported by the evidence. The court concluded that an EIR was not required before the county could issue the permit, and upheld the county's granting of the use permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant religious organization was entitled to use permit to convert a single-family residence into a neighborhood synagogue, as it was not granted an impermissible religious preference by the county board, the decision to grant the permit was supported by substantial evidence, and an environmental impact report was not required before the permit could be granted.

 

1241 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Castillo


No. B035678


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


233 Cal. App. 3d 36; 284 Cal. Rptr. 382; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 922; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6574; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9919



August 9, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Opinion certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I-C, II, III-B, C & D, IV and V-C.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified August 14, 1991 and August 30, 1991.
Petitions for a rehearing were denied August 30, 1991, Reported at 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 1003, and appellants' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 14, 1991. Kennard, J., and George, J., did not participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A706749, Howard J. Schwab, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of conviction are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. A706749 (California), which found them guilty of two counts of kidnapping with bodily harm, and conspiracy to commit kidnapping, claiming that they received in effective assistance counsel, and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellants kidnapped two victims for money. During their ordeal, the victims were repeatedly beaten and injured. After a ransom was paid for one of the kidnapped victims, the police were called in. The police set up a sting operation for the second ransom drop in exchange for the other victim. The police apprehended all appellants, and the second victim was released after undergoing medical treatment. Appellants was charged and convicted with two counts of kidnapping with bodily harm and conspiracy to kidnap. Appellants challenged their conviction, claiming ineffective assistance of counsel, and that the state statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that appellants did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, after they became indigent, and their attorneys request for the county to paid their fees was denied. The court stated that the attorneys did not request to be removed as appellants' counsel, nor did appellants wish to replace their attorneys, and there was no conflict of interest. The court also concluded that the term "bodily harm" was not unconstitutionally vague, as the term was at least as precise as a number of other phrases which had been upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and stated that appellants did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, when the county refused to pay their legal fees once they became indigent, and that the state statute against kidnapping with bodily injury was not unconstitutionally vague, as it was as precise as other phrases that had been upheld.

Arcadia Redevelopment Agency v. Ikemoto


No. B057768


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE.


10 Cal. App. 4th 437; 284 Cal. Rptr. 216; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 904; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9773



August 8, 1991, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted November 11, 1991 (S022924) (See Cal. App. 4th 444)
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 233 Cal. App. 3d 24 and 4 Cal.App.4th 1599)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Supreme Ct. No. S020454; Proceeding in mandamus.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, redevelopment agencies, filed a petition in the California Supreme Court for writ of mandate and requested an immediate stay in their action with respondents, counties and auditor-controllers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, redevelopment agencies, filed a petition for writ of mandate and requested an immediate stay in the California Supreme Court, which transferred the matter to the appellate court. The appellate court found good cause for review and ordered respondents to show cause why the requested relief should not issue, but denied the request for a stay. The court granted an application for permission to file an amicus curiae brief in support of the petition for writ of mandate from petitioners. Petitioners carried out various governmental functions, and respondents, counties and auditor-controllers, collected property taxes on behalf of local taxing agencies. Respondents sent petitioners invoices for property tax administrative costs, and petitioners asserted that the demand was inapplicable, unlawful, and unconstitutional. The court denied the petition for writ of mandate and held that "local jurisdictions" were considered redevelopment agencies based on Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 97's failure to define "local jurisdiction," combined with the legislative intent indicated by the author of the statute. Respondents' notices to petitioners were proper under Cal. Gov't Code § 907.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for writ of mandate of petitioner redevelopment agencies and found in favor of respondents, counties and auditor-controllers, because petitioners qualified as "local jurisdictions" for purposes of paying property tax administrative costs.

Horeczko v. State Bd. of Registration


No. B049131


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


232 Cal. App. 3d 1352; 284 Cal. Rptr. 149; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 919; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6381; 91 Daily Journal DAR 10038



July 31, 1991 


NOTICE:  [***1] Certified for Publication August 9, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: A petition for a rehearing was denied August 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C736748, David P. Yaffe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment appealed from is affirmed. Costs on appeal to the Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an unregistered civil engineer, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied appellant an administrative writ of mandamus to compel respondent, the California Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors, to approve appellant's application for permission to use the title "geotechnical (soils) engineer."


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an unregistered civil engineer, challenged the denial of his application for a writ of administrative mandamus directing respondent California Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors to approve his use of the title "geotechnical (soils) engineer." Appellant contended that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6736.1, restricting the use of the title "soils engineer" to registered engineers, was unconstitutional and unfairly disregarded appellant's 20 years of experience as a soils engineer. The court disagreed. Section 6736.1 reasonably related to a legitimate governmental interest, protection of the public by legislating competency in specialty areas of engineering. Appellant failed to establish an equal protection violation because § 6736.1 did not deny him the opportunity to demonstrate his skills in an attempt to gain status as a registered civil engineer. The striking of an issue concerning appellant's qualifying experience from respondent's statement of issues at the administrative hearing was not prejudicial to appellant because appellant failed to meet the threshold requirement of civil engineer registration. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying a writ of administrative mandamus to appellant engineer. The court concluded that the statute at issue, which restricted the use of the title "soils engineer" to engineers registered by respondent California Board of Registration for Professional Engineers and Land Surveyors, reasonably related to a legitimate governmental interest by legislating competency in specialty areas of engineering.

 

1244 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Adoption of Matthew B.


Nos. A044280, A045711


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


232 Cal. App. 3d 1239; 284 Cal. Rptr. 18; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 871; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6027; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9342



July 30, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for a rehearing were denied August 28, 1991, and August 29, 1991, and appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sonoma County, Nos. 153067 and 153012, Lloyd von der Mehden and Laurence K. Sawyer, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the petition to withdraw consent to adoption (action No. A044280) is affirmed. The appeal from the order denying the motion to vacate the judgment of paternity (action No. A045711) is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, plaintiff surrogate mother challenged judgments from the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California) that denied her petition to vacate defendant father's judgment of paternity, and that denied her petition to withdraw consent to adoption by defendant mother. Plaintiff claimed, among other things, that the trial court erred in not deciding the legality of the surrogate contract and that the paternity judgment was void.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff surrogate mother appealed judgments that denied her petition to vacate defendant father's judgment of paternity and that denied her petition to withdraw her consent to adoption by defendant mother. The court affirmed the judgments. Among the claims rejected by the court was plaintiff's contention that her petition to withdraw consent was improperly denied because the trial court erred in not deciding the legality of the surrogate contract. The court ruled that the contract's legality was properly not addressed by the trial court because, among other things, the parties' performed fully their obligations under it and, in any event, the child's best interests overrode any purported illegality in the contract. In that regard, the court ruled, substantial evidence supported the finding that the child's bests interests were served by not permitting plaintiff to withdraw her consent. The court dismissed plaintiff's appeal regarding the denial of her motion to vacate defendant father's judgment of paternity. The court ruled that because that judgment was entered upon the parties' stipulation and because it was not void, plaintiff was barred from challenging the judgment.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed judgments that denied plaintiff surrogate mother's petitions to withdraw consent to adoption by defendant mother and to vacate defendant father's judgment of paternity. Trial court properly did not decide legality of surrogate contract because parties fully performed the contract and, in any event, child's best interests controlled. Judgment of paternity, entered upon the parties' stipulation, was not void and thus not appealable.

J. L. Thomas, Inc. v. County of Los Angeles


No. B052176


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


232 Cal. App. 3d 916; 283 Cal. Rptr. 815; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 848; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6473; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9034



July 25, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C754360, David P. Yaffe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment denying the petition for writ of mandate is reversed and the trial court is directed to grant the petition for writ of mandate in accordance with the views expressed herein. Appellants are entitled to their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, adult business owners, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied plaintiffs' petition for a writ of mandate in which plaintiffs challenged the decisions of defendants, county, regional planning commission, and board of supervisors, denying an application for a conditional use permit to operate a cabaret featuring live adult entertainment and denying plaintiffs' appeal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, adult business owners, filed suit against defendants, county, regional planning commission, and board of supervisors, because plaintiffs were denied a conditional use permit to operate a cabaret featuring live entertainment. Plaintiffs petitioned for a writ of mandate, challenging defendant board's findings as unsupported by the evidence, and also challenging the relevancy of the findings to the decision to deny the conditional use. The trial court denied the writ, and defendants appealed. The court, in reversing the decision of the trial court, held that the findings of defendant commission did not support the decision. The court found that because of the lack of time limits on the exercise of discretion, the former provisions of the county code pertaining to the issuance of a conditional use permit for adult businesses constituted an invalid prior restraint. The court held that none of the findings of defendant commission specifically addressed the criteria set out in Los Angeles County, Cal., Code §§ 22.56.190, 22.56.090. The court found that the evidence was insufficient to support the irrelevant and inconclusive findings that were made.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment denying the petition for writ of mandate and directed the trial court to grant it in a suit brought by plaintiffs, adult business owners, against defendants, county, regional planning commission, and board of supervisors. The court held that the lack of time limits of the ordinance was an invalid prior restraint, and that the findings of defendant commission did not address the criteria of the ordinances.

In re Charles C.


No. F014198


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


232 Cal. App. 3d 952; 284 Cal. Rptr. 4; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 850; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5855; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9080



July 25, 1991 


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication - Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of Statement of Facts and part 2.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied October 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 66301, Philip A. Silva, Temporary Judge. +


+ Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile found guilty of committing rape in concert, Cal. Penal Code §§ 264.1, 261(2), lewd and lascivious conduct, § 288(a), and unlawful intercourse, §261.5, appealed from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which found him within the provisions of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §602, arguing that he was entitled to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile court found true allegations that defendant juvenile committed rape in concert, Cal. Penal Code, §§ 264.1, 261(2), lewd and lascivious conduct, § 288(a), and unlawful intercourse, § 261.5. The court affirmed, concluding that a jury trial is not constitutionally required in a juvenile court's adjudicative stage. The court rejected defendant's argument that because any person over 18 years of age charged with an offense which may result in imprisonment for more than six months is entitled to a jury trial, the fact that defendant was not entitled to a jury trial meant his commitment could not extend beyond six months past the age of majority. The court also rejected defendant's argument that he was entitled to a jury trial because the juvenile court had extended jurisdiction pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §607(b) and his confinement would carryover into adulthood. The court reasoned that the underlying purpose of the juvenile system remained sufficiently distinct from the adult criminal system to support confinement at California Youth Authority rehabilitative programs into adulthood for juvenile offenses without a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial finding that a jury trial is not constitutionally required in a juvenile court's adjudicative stage and that the fact that a juvenile offender may be committed for a term extending into his adulthood likewise does not warrant a jury trial.

Cal. Auto. Assigned Risk Plan v. Garamendi


No. B047146


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


232 Cal. App. 3d 904; 283 Cal. Rptr. 562; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 852; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5916; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9029



July 25, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A petition for a rehearing was denied August 20, 1991, and respondents' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied October 17, 1991. George, J., did not participate therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C-704876, Miriam A. Vogel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: That portion of the judgment declaring that section 1861.05, subdivisions (b) and (c), and sections 1861.06 through 1861.09, inclusive, apply to hearings to set rates for automobile liability policies issued under CAARP is reversed. The judgment is affirmed in all other respects. The commissioner shall recover his costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, insurance commissioner, state, and attorney general, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which declared that certain provisions of Proposition 103, Cal. Ins. Code §§ 1861.01-1861.14, applied to automobile insurance policies issued under the California Automobile Assigned Risk Plan, Cal. Ins. Code § 11620 et seq.; Cal. Code Regs. tit.10, § 2400 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, risk plan and indemnity company, filed a complaint against defendants, insurance commissioner, state, and attorney general, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from the provisions of Proposition 103, which was made part of the insurance code in Cal. Ins. Code §§ 1861.01-1861.14. The trial court interpreted the new statute. The court reversed the portion of the judgment that declared that Cal. Ins. Code § 1861.05(b) and (c) and §§ 1861.06-1861.09 applied to hearings to set rates for automobile liability policies under the California Automobile Assigned Risk Plan (CAARP), Cal. Ins. Code § 11620 et seq.; Cal. Code Regs. tit. 10, § 2400 et seq. The court held that Proposition 103 was intended to impose significant controls upon the setting of rates for insurance in the voluntary market and was not intended to alter procedures for establishing the uniform rate set by defendant insurance commissioner for assigned-risk insurance. The court held that the trial court erred in declaring that § 1861.05(b) and (c) and §§ 1861.06-1861.09 applied to hearings to set rates for automobile liability policies issued under CAARP. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that certain portions of the insurance code that were added by Proposition 103 applied to hearings to set rates for automobile liability policies issued under the California Automobile Assigned Risk Plan. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects in declaratory action filed by plaintiffs, risk plan and indemnity company, against defendants, insurance commissioner, state, and attorney general.

 

1248 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. McGee


No. A051882


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Five


232 Cal. App. 3d 620; 283 Cal. Rptr. 528; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 823; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5720; 91 Daily Journal DAR 9023



July 19, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Mendocino County, No. C10219, Ronald R. Combest, Judge. +


+ Judge of the Round Valley Justice Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The trial court is directed to vacate its order reinstating defendant's guilty plea and to enter an order withdrawing the plea. The court is directed to set a new trial date.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Mendocino County (California) convicting him of sexually molesting a child under the age of 14, arguing that the court had no authority to reconsider and vacate an earlier ruling that set aside his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's authority to reconsider and to vacate an earlier ruling that set aside his guilty plea to the sexual molestation of a child under the age of 14. Defendant contended that the trial court lost jurisdiction once it entered an order that allowed him to withdraw his plea. The court held that the trial court had no authority to reinstate defendant's guilty plea without his acquiescence. Cal. Penal Code § 1018 permits the defendant, and only the defendant, to enter a guilty plea or make a motion to withdraw a previously entered plea. The language permits no interpretation that would allow the prosecutor to make a motion, or the trial court on its own motion, to reinstate a guilty plea after it is withdrawn. Therefore, the trial court was directed to vacate its order reinstating defendant's guilty plea and to enter an order withdrawing the plea.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed because the court had no authority to reinstate defendant's guilty plea to sexually molesting a child under the age of 14 without his acquiescence. The applicable statute permitted only defendant to enter a guilty plea or make a motion to withdraw a previous plea.

Elysium Inst. v. County of L.A.


No. B031797


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Seven


232 Cal. App. 3d 408; 283 Cal. Rptr. 688; 1991 Cal. App. LEXIS 829; 91 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5682; 91 Daily Journal DAR 8743



July 18, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' petition for review by the Supreme Court was denied October 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C598750, Norman R. Dowds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified to include the declaration that County Code sections 22.08.140 and 22.24.150 are unconstitutional as applied to appellants' property herein; in all other respects the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nudist camp sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied plaintiff's petition for writ of mandamus after defendant county denied plaintiff's application for nonconforming use permit to continue operation of the camp.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff nudist camp appealed from a judgment denying its petition for writ of mandamus challenging defendant county's denial of its permit application and the constitutionality of Los Angeles County Zoning Ordinance No. 10,366 (10,366) pertaining to nudist camps. Prior to enactment of the ordinance, nudist camps were permitted in zone A-1. The ordinance restricted nudist camps to zone A-2 with a conditional use permit. The court found no compelling interest under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1 to justify the inclusion of a private home within the definition of nudist camp. Furthermore, the restriction of nudist camps to the A-2 zone constituted a denial of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7. However, challenges to the conditional use permits were meritless because they failed to establish that integration of various uses within a particular zone did not constitute a legitimate interest, bearing a reasonable relation to the public welfare. The court held that while plaintiff was entitled to a declaration that Los Angeles County Code §§ 22.08.140 and 22.24.150 were unconstitutional, the denial of the permit was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying plaintiff nudist camp's petition for writ of mandamus because, although certain restrictions were unconstitutional, defendant county's conditional use restrictions were valid because nudists failed to show that such conditional use did not constitute a legitimate interest, bearing a reasonable relation to public welfare.
